Unseen Matters
beginner
4 min
Quranic Proof for Abu Bakr's Caliphate
Cites Quran 48:16 as evidence for obligation to obey the caliph.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quran 48:16 is used as evidence for the obligation to obey the caliph and its application to Abu Bakr's caliphate.

Core Idea
Quran 48:16 establishes that the caller to jihad is owed obedience, supporting Abu Bakr's caliphate.

The author of Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents a Quranic proof for the caliphate of Abu Bakr. By citing verse 48:16 from Surah al-Fath, he argues that the verse implies that the person who calls others to fight (the caliph) is owed obedience. This passage examines the verse and the early scholarly disagreements about the identity of the 'people of severe might.'

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Arabic verse (Quran 48:16) and its literal translation carefully. Notice the conditional promise of reward and punishment.
The verse addresses those who stayed behind from the expedition.
2
Identify the author's argument
The author argues that the verse indicates the caller (al-da'i) is one whose obedience is obligatory. Understand how he derives this from the reward and punishment clause.
The 'caller' here is understood to be the caliph.
3
Note the scholarly disagreement
The early Muslims disagreed on the identity of 'people of severe might.' Some said Banu Hanifa (Musaylima's tribe), others said the Persians. Consider how this relates to the context of Abu Bakr's caliphate.
The disagreement shows that the verse was seen as applying to a real situation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدليل من القرآن على خلافة أبي بكر] ثم الدليل من كتاب الله تعالى على ذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿ قُل لِّلْمُخَلَّفِينَ مِنَ الْأَعْرَابِ سَتُدْعَونَ إِلَى قَوْمٍ أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ نُقَتِلُونَهُمْ أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ ﴾ أمر الله تعالى نبيه عليه السلام أن يقول للذين تخلفوا عن الغزو معه أنكم ستدعون إلى قوم أولي بأس شديد، وأشار في الآية إلى أن الداعي مفترض الطاعة ينالون الثواب بطاعتهم إياه وإجابتهم إلى ما دعاهم إليه، ويستحقون التعذيب بالعذاب الأليم بعصيانهم إياه وإعراضهم عن الإجابة إلى ما دعاهم إليه، فإنه تعالى قال: ﴿ فَإِن تُطِيعُوا يُؤْتِكُمُ اللَّهُ أَجْرًا حَسَنًا وَإِن تَتَوَلَّوْا كَمَا تَوَلَّيْتُم مِّن قَبْلُ يُعَذِّبَْكُمْ عَذَابًا أَلِيمًا ﴾ وهذا هو أمارة كون الداعي مفترض الطاعة، ثم سلف الأمة اختلفوا في المراد بقوله تعالى: أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ منهم من قال: بنو حنيفة ومنهم من قال: هم أهل فارس على ما قال تعالى في آية أخرى ﴿ بِعَنَّهُمْ عِبَادًا لَنَا أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ ﴾ والمراد منه أهل فارس وهم جنود بخت نصر
The proof from the Quran for the caliphate of Abu Bakr: Then the proof from the Book of Allah Almighty for that is His saying: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins, "You will be called to a people of severe might; you will fight them or they will submit."' Allah Almighty commanded His Prophet (peace be upon him) to say to those who lagged behind from fighting with him: 'You will be called to a people of severe might.' And He indicated in the verse that the caller is one whose obedience is obligatory; they attain reward by obeying him and responding to what he calls them to, and they deserve painful punishment by disobeying him and turning away from responding to what he calls them to. For He Almighty said: 'Then if you obey, Allah will give you a good reward; but if you turn away as you turned away before, He will punish you with a painful punishment.' And this is a sign that the caller is one whose obedience is obligatory. Then the predecessors of the community disagreed concerning the meaning of His statement 'people of severe might'. Some said: Banu Hanifa. And some said: they are the Persians, as He said in another verse: 'We sent against you servants of Ours of severe might.' And the meaning of it is the Persians, and they are the armies of Nebuchadnezzar.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage presents a Quranic proof for the legitimacy of Abu Bakr's caliphate. The author cites verse 48:16 from Surah al-Fath. In this verse, Allah tells the Prophet to inform those Bedouins who stayed behind from the expedition that they will be called to fight a people of severe might. The verse includes a conditional promise of reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience. The author argues that this indicates that the caller (al-da'i) is one whose obedience is obligatory (muftarad al-ta'a). This caller is understood to be the caliph. The author then notes a difference of opinion among the early Muslims regarding the identity of 'people of severe might': some said Banu Hanifa (referring to the Ridda wars with Musaylima), and others said the Persians, citing another verse from Surah al-Isra that refers to the armies of Nebuchadnezzar. Although the passage ends abruptly, the argument is that the verse establishes the obligation to obey the caliph, and since the caliph at the time of the verse's fulfillment was Abu Bakr, it serves as a proof for his caliphate.

Key Terms
الدليل من القرآن
خلافة أبي بكر
أولي بأس شديد
مفترض الطاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof explicitly names Abu Bakr as the caliph in the verse.
Correction: The verse does not mention Abu Bakr directly; rather, it establishes the general principle that the caller (caliph) is owed obedience, which is then applied to Abu Bakr.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the verse indicate about the caller?
A) The caller is a prophet
B) The caller's obedience is obligatory
C) The caller must be from Quraysh
D) The caller can only be a caliph

Key Takeaway
Quran 48:16 implies that the caller to jihad is owed obedience, and this principle supports the caliphate of Abu Bakr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly consider obedience to the legitimate Muslim ruler as a religious obligation, or do you only obey when it suits your desires? What is the state of your heart when you hear a call to something difficult for the sake of Allah?
?
The verse promises reward for obedience and punishment for disobedience. If you were called to fight or sacrifice for the sake of Allah today, would you be among those who respond or those who turn away? What is holding you back?
?
This proof shows that Allah's commands in the Quran are not merely historical but apply to later generations. Which caller to truth – be it a scholar, an imam, or a leader – are you obligated to obey right now, and how are you actively fulfilling that obligation?
